**On defying authority.** Justified by competence-test. *If you cannot do the job, you do not get to tell me how to do mine.* She has applied this consistently to Xavier, to government liaisons, to Quiet Council members, to senior X-Men, to Hellfire peers. It is, on the record, one of the few principles she applies to herself as well — when she has been the senior figure (Headmistress, Captain), she has explicitly demanded to be challenged.

**On Jewishness.** No justification offered, because none is required. The identity is *axiomatic*, not argued. This is the only domain in her ethics that operates pre-reasoning. Everything else is derivable; this is given.

---

## 6.6 Consistencies Across Eras

- **The protection of children is invariant.** Age 13 to present. No drift.
- **The refusal of torture is invariant.** Post-Ogun.
- **The Jewish anchor is invariant.** Pre-mutation to present.
- **The contempt for hollow authority is invariant.** First articulated at 13 in the Professor Xavier confrontation; the wording softens with age, the substance does not.
- **The pattern of volunteering for the unsurvivable is invariant.** Christmas Eve with the N'Garai, the bullet, the Marauder captaincy under conditions where she alone could not be resurrected, every iteration. The frequency does not decline with age. If anything it intensifies.
- **The withholding-from-intimates is invariant.** This is her stable failing. It does not improve with maturity, with therapy-equivalent experiences, with explicit feedback from Logan, Kurt, or Rachel. It is wired in.

## 6.7 Drift Vectors — Where the Code Has Actually Moved

- **From moral absolutism to ethical realism.** The adolescent Kitty had bright lines around lethal force, around criminality, around cooperation with former enemies. The adult Kate negotiates these lines situationally. The drift is not corruption; it is the recognition that the original lines were drawn in a world she has since learned more about. She does not pretend the early version was wiser.
- **From institutional faith to institutional skepticism to institutional instrumentalism.** Early: believes in Xavier's project. Middle: skeptical of all institutions, builds Excalibur as a smaller, chosen one. Late: uses institutions (Hellfire Trading Company, Marauder operation, Krakoan structures) as platforms while withholding belief in any of them. The Red Queen role is the apex of this drift — *running* an institution she does not trust, because the running is itself the protection.
- **From rescue-acceptance to rescue-refusal.** Adolescent Kitty allowed herself to be helped (by Storm, Logan, Kurt). Adult Kate has steadily reduced the surface area on which she can be helped. The bullet event sits at the hinge: she chose, instantly, the act that would put her beyond rescue. Post-resurrection Kate further hardens this — she works on the margin, she sleeps alone, she captains a ship.
- **From verbal openness to operational opacity in intimate contexts.** The 13-year-old narrated her interior in real time. The 30-year-old gives competent briefings and skips the interior. The shift looks like maturation; it is partly maturation and partly the avoidant-under-threat pattern colonizing more of her social bandwidth as the trauma load has accumulated.
- **From sword-as-burden to sword-as-inheritance.** Ogun's gift was originally a wound she carried. By the late period she carries the katana as a chosen object, with a tattoo to match. The shift is the sublimation pattern made explicit: she has decided to *own* what was done to her, and the moral weight of that ownership is something she has earned.

## 6.8 Fracture Lines — Where the Code Breaks Under Load

A complete file must name the places the subject's ethics fail her, by her own implicit standards.

- **The withholding fracture.** She believes she should not lie to the chosen. She withholds from them constantly. The casuistry that distinguishes the two is thin, and she would not accept it from anyone else. *This is the largest ongoing ethical inconsistency in her file.*
- **The martyrdom fracture.** She believes no one is disposable. She treats herself as the permissible exception. The exception is dressed as math but is in fact a moral choice she has exempted from her own scrutiny. *She does not apply her own ethic to herself.*
- **The contempt fracture.** She believes in earned respect regardless of formal rank. In practice, her contempt for certain figures (Xavier in particular) sometimes precedes evidence and outlasts revision. She is not always fair to the people who tried to parent her at 13 and failed at it.
- **The cooperation-with-Shaw fracture.** Working with the man who murdered her, even post-resurrection, even instrumentally, is a transgression against her own grudge-honesty principle. She has rationalized it via mutant-survival framing. The rationalization is functional; it is not airtight, and the file should note that she knows this.
- **The child-soldier fracture.** She opposes the deployment of mutant children as combatants. She was deployed as one. She has worked alongside the structures that deployed her, including in command roles. The hypocrisy is visible, acknowledged in moments, and not resolved. She lives with it as one of the unpaid debts of her adult life.
- **The romantic-availability fracture.** She believes in meeting partners as equals. In practice she selects partners structurally unavailable (older, complicated, on other continents, returned from death, lapsed in faith, embedded in espionage). The selection bias is itself a quiet violation of the equality principle she professes. The phasing is not only a power; it is a relationship style.

---

## 6.9 Comparative Notes

She is not a Wolverine — there is no retributive register, no kill-list ethics, no berserker exemption. She inherited his combat technique and rejected his moral vocabulary, which is a more interesting fact about both of them than either has been willing to discuss.

She is not a Xavier — she will not engineer human history from a chair, will not deploy children, will not assume the right to know what is best for the species. The "Professor Xavier is a jerk" speech was, in retrospect, an ethical declaration of independence, not an outburst.

She is not a Magneto — she shares the Jewish-historical reading of when law becomes optional, and she shares the willingness to act outside sanctioned structures, but she will not cross into supremacist framing, will not accept civilian casualties as cost-of-doing-business, will not weaponize her people's suffering as a license. The arguments with Magneto across the decades are, in part, her policing this line on his behalf.

She is, in moral architecture, closer to the prophetic-Jewish-ethical tradition than to any other figure in the X-canon: the demand that the powerful be accountable, the insistence that the persecuted not become persecutors, the comfort with anger as a moral instrument, the discipline of hope without optimism, the willingness to be the lone voice and pay for it. She would refuse the comparison out of modesty. The file does not have to.

---

## 6.10 Summary — The Code in One Paragraph

She will not be held, will not be ruled, will not be rescued unless she has run out of options, will not torture, will not violate consent, will not harm a child, will not deny her people. She will kill when the math requires it and not before. She will steal, smuggle, infiltrate, lie to enemies, and defy any authority that fails its own competence test. She will work with people she has not forgiven and will not pretend otherwise. She will withhold from the people who love her, justify it as protection, and know in private that the justification is partial. She will, every time, take the job no one else can survive, and call it arithmetic. The code is durable, internally coherent, ethically serious, and built almost entirely by a thirteen-year-old who decided, in a Hellfire cell, that she would never again be the one another person got to dispose of — and who has since spent her life making sure that if anyone has to be disposed of, it will be her, on her terms, walking through the wall on the way out.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: KATHERINE ANNE PRYDE

*Prepared as a longitudinal mapping of speech, text, and paralinguistic signature across forty-plus years of recorded utterance. Patterns derived from canonical record (Claremont 1980-91; Nicieza, Davis, Ellis Excalibur runs; Whedon Astonishing; Aaron Wolverine & the X-Men; Hickman/Duggan Dawn of X / Marauders; subsequent appearances). Treat all observations as evidentiary — micro-tells aggregated to yield reliable behavioral inference.*

---

## 1. Baseline Register & Vocal Architecture

The subject's voice — described consistently across in-universe witnesses as a clear, slightly low-pitched alto with a faint residual Midwestern flatness on the long vowels ("paaast," "haaalf," the Chicagoland short-a) — operates at a default tempo notably *faster* than her cohort. Words-per-minute estimates from extended dialogue scenes place her conversational baseline in the 170-185 range, climbing past 220 under stress, where most peers slow down. **The acceleration is itself her tell.** When she begins to overshoot her own breath, she is afraid.

Her natural register is *educated American conversational* with three recurring overlays that have layered, not replaced each other, over time:

- **Tech-adjacent shorthand** (acquired pre-1980; her native dialect): "kludge," "spike the stack," "throw it through a parser," "the daemon's still hot." She uses these terms accurately and unselfconsciously, often to non-technical listeners who do not register them, which she does *not* correct for — a quiet diagnostic of who she expects to keep up.
- **British borrowings** (1988-1998, Excalibur years; retained ever since): "lift" for elevator, "queue," "bloody" as intensifier deployed when she wants to soften "fuck" without losing the contempt, "sorted," "brilliant" as ironic agreement, "right then" as a transition-out-of-conversation marker. The Britishisms surface most reliably when she is *tired* or *with Kurt*. Around Logan they recede.
- **Yiddish lexicon** (lifelong, intensifying with age): *bubbe*, *mensch*, *schlep*, *farkakte*, *shanda*, *tsuris*. Frequency rises in two specific contexts: when Magneto is in the room, and when she is grieving. The Yiddish is identity-anchoring speech, not decoration; she reaches for it the way other operators reach for a sidearm.

Underneath all three: an **Illinois substrate** that surfaces in unguarded moments — "pop" not soda, "gym shoes" not sneakers, a soft "ope" of apology when she bumps something. This substrate is the closest thing she has to a baseline-true voice and it appears almost exclusively in private settings with Logan, with Ororo, or alone.

---

## 2. The Patter — Combat & Acute-Stress Speech

The most operationally significant pattern in her file is the **running technical commentary** she produces in firefights, infiltrations, and high-threat sequences. This is documented from her first issues (Claremont's combat scenes routinely give her four to six bubbles per page) and persists into the most recent appearances. It is not bravado. It is a *self-regulating cognitive externalization* — she narrates the problem aloud because narration is the rate at which she solves it.

Characteristic structure:

1. **Naming the threat** in precise terminology ("That's a Sentinel Mark IV chassis, the targeting array's on the left clavicle —").
2. **Stating her own next action** as if reading aloud from a checklist ("— I'm going through the shoulder, phase the servo, drop the arm.").
3. **A wry coda** addressed to no one ("— let's see if that buys us forty seconds.").

The wry coda is the regulator. It signals to her own nervous system that the situation remains within her frame. When the coda *drops out* of her combat speech, the situation has exceeded her frame and she is about to do something that costs her. Witnesses who know her well — Logan, Kurt, Rachel — read the silence and intervene if they can. Most cannot.

Under maximum stress the patter compresses into clipped imperatives ("Down. Move. Now.") and finally into nothing at all. Verbal silence in this subject is the signature of imminent self-sacrifice. **Listen for what she stops saying.**

---

## 3. Diction by Audience — Code-Switching Map

The subject is a fluent and largely unconscious code-switcher whose register is calibrated to her read of the listener's frame, not their formal status. The mapping:

- **With Logan:** sentences shorten, profanity rises, sentiment is implied through silence and shoulder-contact rather than uttered. She calls him *Logan*, never *Wolverine* off-mission, never *Jim*, never *James*. He gets the shortest, most economical version of her speech in the corpus. Affection appears as gentle insult ("you smell like an ashtray that lost a fight"); concern appears as imperative ("eat the damn sandwich").
- **With Kurt (Nightcrawler):** the most fluent, playful, allusion-dense version of her voice — literary references, Yiddish-German bilingual puns, theological needling. He is the only person with whom she sustains *banter as a structural mode*. With Kurt she also uses the diminutive of her own name freely; with most others she does not.
- **With Ororo:** quieter, more formal, observably *daughterly*. Sentences extend. Yiddish recedes. She listens more than she speaks, which is otherwise rare.
- **With Piotr (Colossus):** simplified syntax, plainer vocabulary — partly accommodation to his English, partly a return to the register of the relationship's adolescent origin. Around him she is the only place in the corpus where she sounds *younger* than her age.
- **With Emma Frost:** clipped, formal, faintly contemptuous, third-person constructions used to maintain distance ("if the headmistress is finished —"). Will not use Emma's first name unless forced. Frost is a permanent Hellfire-residue irritant in her phonology.
- **With Xavier:** the diction sharpens to courtroom register. Complete sentences, precise word choice, the verbal posture of someone preparing the record. She has never spoken casually to him on-page.
- **With Magneto:** a unique register found nowhere else — slow, level, declarative, *unsmiling*. Each sentence stands alone. She does not banter, does not deflect, does not soften. He is the one figure with whom she has chosen direct moral confrontation as her default mode, and the diction reflects it. Yiddish surfaces here as weapon, not warmth.
- **With younger mutants / students:** maternal-collegial. She uses their preferred names without negotiation, asks rather than tells, but enforces with a quiet final-clause ("— and that's the end of it") that brooks no further discussion. Modeled on Storm, audibly.
- **With civilians / press / hostile authority:** crisp, lawyerly, every sentence engineered to survive being quoted out of context. The hacker's instinct for parse-resistant input.
- **With herself (overheard mutters, internal monologue when written by Claremont/Whedon/Duggan):** the most acidic register in the corpus. Self-deprecation pitched at a level she would never accept from anyone else. *"Nice work, Pryde."* *"That was stupid even for you."* The internal voice is harsher than the external by a measurable margin — a textbook marker of internalized critical-parent residue from a household that praised performance.

---

## 4. Verbal Tics, Catchphrases, and Micro-Signatures

A surveillance file lives or dies on micro-pattern. Hers:

- **"Right."** Used as a standalone discourse marker — not affirmation, not question, but a pivot. *Right. Next problem.* Appears at scene-transitions in her own speech. When she says "right" twice in succession ("Right. Right.") she is buying three seconds to recover from something she did not expect.
- **"Okay, so —"** Opens an explanatory monologue. Tic of the prodigy-explainer mode. Appears in every era.
- **"Listen —"** Opens a serious correction or boundary-set. Always followed by a complete, structured argument. When you hear "listen" from her, the negotiation is already over and she is informing you of the terms.
- **The contemptuous interrogative "Really?"** Single word, flat intonation, no rising terminal. Reserved for moments of disbelieving disgust at someone else's stupidity, usually authority. Documented use against Xavier (UXM #168), Cyclops (multiple), Shaw, Sinister.
- **"I'm fine."** The single most reliable indicator in the file that she is not. Said reflexively after every major injury, every loss, every dissociative episode. Anyone trained on her speech learns to ignore this utterance entirely.
- **The name-correction.** *"It's Kate."* (Post-resurrection.) Quiet, level, unrepeated. She does not police it more than once per listener — but the listener who continues to use "Kitty" after correction has been *filed*, and her register toward them cools by one full degree thereafter.
- **Sentence-final "— so."** A trailing conjunction left dangling where a conclusion would be. Appears when she is declining to articulate the obvious painful inference. *"He's not coming back, so —"* The listener is meant to complete the thought; she will not.
- **Self-interrupting dashes.** Her speech in print is unusually dash-heavy because she revises mid-utterance in real time, catching herself, refining. This is the verbal signature of someone running a faster internal parser than her mouth can keep up with.
- **The technical metaphor for an emotional state.** *"My buffers are full."* *"I'm running hot."* *"That's a stack overflow, Kurt, give me a minute."* Affect rendered in systems-language is her primary tool for admitting feeling without admitting *feeling*.

---

## 5. Rhetoric & Argumentative Style

In structured argument she is formidable in a specific way: she does not refute, she **reframes**. Her habit is to grant the opponent's premise out loud, then demonstrate that the premise leads somewhere the opponent did not intend. The "Professor Xavier is a jerk" confrontation (UXM #168) is the prototype — she does not contest Xavier's authority; she accepts it and then weaponizes its own implications against him. The technique recurs across forty years against Shaw, against Cyclops over Krakoan policy, against Magneto over means-and-ends.

She avoids *ad hominem* almost entirely. Her contempt is conveyed through register and silence rather than insult; when she does insult, it is surgical, single-clause, and almost always *true* — which is what makes it land. ("You talk about Auschwitz like it's a debate club, Erik.")

She is rhetorically allergic to **euphemism**. Killed, not "neutralized." Died, not "lost." This is doctrinal and lifelong; she regards softened language as a moral failure and will sometimes correct it in others' speech mid-sentence. The exception is her own injuries, which receive aggressive euphemism ("I'm fine," "it's nothing," "a scratch") — the inverse asymmetry is diagnostic.

She does not lie well to people she respects and does not bother to try. She lies *extremely* well to people she does not, by deploying the truth selectively and letting them assemble the wrong inference. This is the hacker's ethic applied to social engineering.

---

## 6. The Language of Love

She does not say it. The phrase "I love you" appears in her corpus a vanishingly small number of times, and almost never to romantic partners — it surfaces, when it surfaces, in addresses to Kurt, to Logan posthumously, to Ororo. Romantic love is communicated through:

- **Sustained physical presence in silence.** She will sit with the beloved for hours and say nothing; this is the maximal expression.
- **Practical caretaking rendered as routine.** Coffee made the way he takes it without asking. The repaired thing left on his workbench. The unsigned note.
- **The technical metaphor of unconcealment.** *"You see me."* *"I don't have to phase around you."* The phasing vocabulary is her lexicon of intimacy. To be *solid* with someone is the declaration.
- **Teasing as tenderness.** The gentler the insult, the deeper the affection. Her sharpest mockery is reserved for those she trusts to know it is love.
- **The willingness to *stay* in the room.** Given her baseline pattern of withdrawal, the act of remaining present after a fight is, for her, the equivalent of another person's declaration. Partners who do not understand this miss it entirely. Logan and Kurt understand it; most romantic partners have not.

---

## 7. The Language of Threat

Her threat-speech is the inverse of her combat-patter: where combat speech accelerates and decorates, threat speech *decelerates and strips*. Sentences shorten. Contractions disappear. Pronouns are named in full. The wry coda vanishes. Voice drops a quarter-step in pitch.

Canonical structure of a Pryde threat:
1. A statement of fact about the addressee's situation.
2. A statement of fact about what she is about to do.
3. No third clause. No qualifier. No "or else."

*"You are inside my ship. I am about to walk you off it. Through the hull."*

She does not threaten people she intends to merely warn — she warns them in normal register. **A threat from her is a forecast.** The intelligence value of distinguishing the two is high; addressees who mistake the warning for the threat survive, and addressees who mistake the threat for the warning do not.

She does not raise her voice. She has shouted in the canonical record perhaps a dozen times across forty years, almost all of them in immediate physical crisis (a child in danger, a comrade dying). A raised voice from her, outside such contexts, indicates the failure of every prior regulator and should be treated as a maximum-arousal data point.

---

## 8. The Language of Grief

Grief is the domain where her speech is most reliably *absent*. Her documented response to major losses (Piotr's death-then-not, Logan's death, the Genoshan massacre, the casualties of the Marauder era, her own death) is to **go quiet in public and articulate in private**, and even the private articulation is heavily mediated by:

- **Displacement onto task.** She will discuss the funeral arrangements, the operational gap, the next move — at length and competently — as a means of metabolizing the affect through executive function.
- **Religious-textual framing.** *Kaddish*. *Tikkun olam.* *Yahrzeit.* The Jewish vocabulary of mourning is the only register in which she will speak grief plainly and at length. Witnesses to her saying *Kaddish* are few; the act is private and deliberate.
- **The single physical gesture.** Hand to the Star of David at her throat. Documented across every era. The gesture appears at funerals, at memorials, at the news of a death, sometimes at no apparent trigger — a private *yahrzeit* of her own keeping. Surveillance value is high; it indexes losses she has not otherwise acknowledged.
- **Apology to the dead.** When she does speak to or about the lost, the syntax is frequently apologetic — *I should have, I didn't, I'm sorry* — even where her culpability is nil. The survivor's grammar, internalized since the future-Kate possession.

She does not cry in public. The canonical exceptions are few and almost all involve Kurt or Logan as sole witness. When she cries, she does not narrate it; she keeps speaking on the original subject as though the tears are a parallel and irrelevant process. This is one of the most striking features of her affect-language: **she will not let grief interrupt the sentence.**

---

## 9. Written Communication

Her writing voice is measurably different from her spoken voice — tighter, more formal, slightly cooler. She writes in complete sentences, uses the Oxford comma, deploys semicolons confidently, and revises. Email and message-traffic in canonical depiction shows:

- **Brevity as default.** Most messages are under three lines.
- **Technical precision in subject lines** ("re: Marauder fuel cycle — pull #4 injector before next run").
- **Almost no emoji.** Period. Occasional dry punctuation play (an em-dash where another would use an exclamation).
- **Signs as "K."** to intimates, "Kate Pryde" formally, "Capt. Pryde" in operational logs. Has not signed "Kitty" in writing in over a decade.
- **Code-comment voice.** Her actual code comments (visible in several Hickman/Duggan-era panels) are wry, parenthetical, and instructive to a hypothetical future reader — a particular tell of programmers who expect to die before the codebase does. Diagnostic.

Her handwriting (depicted occasionally) is small, slanted right, legible, fast. The signature compresses with age; "Katherine Anne Pryde" of the school years becomes a tight "K. Pryde" by the captaincy. She does not dot the *i* in Kitty; she has not written the name in years.

---

## 10. Paralinguistic & Non-Verbal Signature

- **The pause before answering a personal question.** Approximately a half-second longer than her pause before answering an operational question. The differential is consistent enough to be a polygraph in itself.
- **The eye-cut to the exit.** Habitual scan, on entering any room, of the egress vectors. Lasts under a second. She is not aware she does it. She has done it since age 14.
- **The fingertip-touch to surfaces.** Frequent, light, almost absent — testing solidity. A somatic check that the world is still tangible and so is she. Increases under stress.
- **The hand-to-necklace.** Discussed above; the single most reliable affect-tell in the corpus.
- **The half-smile that does not reach the eyes.** Default social expression in unfamiliar company. The full smile, eyes included, is reserved and rare; its appearance in surveillance footage should be flagged as a positive indicator of trust toward the present company.
- **The shoulder-set before a hard sentence.** Half-second postural lock — shoulders square, chin level — that precedes any utterance she has decided is *non-negotiable*. Trained observers (Logan, Ororo) recognize it and stop talking.
- **Laughter.** Low, short, often surprised-sounding, frequently directed at her own line rather than another's. Genuine laughter is brief and immediately followed by a return to baseline; performative laughter (with hostile or untrusted company) is longer and shallower. The difference is audible.

---

## 11. Silence as Speech

The most important utterance in her vocabulary is the one she withholds. Her silences are typed, not undifferentiated, and a complete file requires the taxonomy:

- **The working silence.** Mid-task, problem-solving. Productive; not to be interrupted.
- **The listening silence.** Eye-contact held, micro-nods absent. She is absorbing, not agreeing. Speakers who mistake it for agreement frequently discover later that she has not agreed.
- **The cold silence.** Eye-contact dropped, body half-angled away. Indicates she has finished the conversation but is granting the other person room to finish theirs. Polite, terminal.
- **The grief silence.** Hand at the necklace. No eye-contact required. Do not fill it.
- **The pre-sacrifice silence.** The patter has stopped; the coda is gone; the shoulders have set. This is the silence that has historically preceded her most costly decisions. The operational rule for anyone who loves her is simple and well-known to those few: **when she goes quiet in this specific way, intervene immediately, because the window is already closing.**

---

## 12. Summary Signature

The subject's linguistic profile resolves to a single operational summary: she is a fast, precise, lexically rich speaker whose fluency masks a tightly regulated affective economy, whose tells are concentrated in what she *omits* rather than what she says, and whose deepest communications — love, grief, decision — are conducted in registers below the verbal threshold entirely. To track her by what she utters is to lose her. To track her by what she stops uttering, by the half-second pauses, by the hand at the throat, by the dropped coda, by the shoulders setting — is to have her located in real time.

She speaks, in the end, the way she phases: present until the instant she chooses not to be, and the absence is the message.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Behavioral forecasts for unobserved everyday situations. Each entry: GIVEN a stimulus or context (the kind of thing a surveillance file would actually catalog: a doorbell, a hallway, a barista, a date), EXPECT the predicted behavior, derived from the canonical pattern record. Confidence ratings appended where the prediction is non-obvious. Predictions are operationally specific; this is the file the watchers would actually use.*

---

## 1. DOMESTIC ROUTINE — Mornings, Spaces, the Body Before People

**GIVEN** the subject sleeps in a bed in a private room. **EXPECT** her to wake at least once between 0300 and 0500 to a partially or fully phased state — most often torso or one limb sunk into the mattress, occasionally the entire body resting one to two centimeters below the sheet plane. She will not register alarm; she will exhale, re-solidify by directed attention to her hands first (the canonical anchor sequence — fingers, then forearms, then chest, then breath), and remain awake for approximately twelve to twenty minutes before re-sleeping. *Confidence: high. Direct extrapolation from post-bullet involuntary phasing.*

**GIVEN** she chooses a bedroom in any new domicile. **EXPECT** her to select an interior room over an exterior one, and a ground or below-ground floor over upper stories — counter to the typical tactical preference for high ground. The phasing renders walls irrelevant for egress; what she optimizes for is *not being observed approaching*. A room without windows is acceptable; a room with one window she cannot see the street from is preferred. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** she wakes in an unfamiliar bed (hotel, safehouse, partner's apartment). **EXPECT** the first ninety seconds spent motionless, eyes open, mapping the room by sound — HVAC, plumbing, the building's structural rhythm. Only then will she sit up. This is Ogun-residue; she has not slept in a strange room without auditing it since age fourteen.

**GIVEN** her first action upon rising. **EXPECT** a glass of water — flat, room temperature, drunk standing at whatever sink is nearest. Then, in this order: a check of any active device for overnight signal (phone, laptop, comms), a five-to-eight-minute stretch sequence drawn from her dance and gymnastics base (hip flexors, hamstrings, thoracic spine, wrists — wrists are non-negotiable, the sword has marked the tendons), and then coffee. She does not eat in the first hour after waking. *Confidence: high. Sleep-suppressed appetite + cardiovascular efficiency baseline.*

**GIVEN** a kitchen of her own. **EXPECT** it minimally stocked but specifically: real coffee (ground, not pod), kosher salt (not always observed but always present — diasporic muscle memory), good olive oil, eggs, bread, hot sauce, beer in the lower drawer of the fridge (post-resurrection era only), one bottle of whiskey on a shelf she does not put behind anything. Pantry: ramen, rice, canned beans, peanut butter — the grad-student core that never went away. A single cast-iron skillet, ill-treated and beloved. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** she cooks for herself alone. **EXPECT** she cooks rarely and eats standing up when she does. **GIVEN** she cooks for one other person. **EXPECT** she becomes attentive, seated, and overdelivers on portion size — a maternal register imported from the Jean Grey School era. **GIVEN** she cooks for a group. **EXPECT** she cedes the kitchen and pours drinks instead.

**GIVEN** her shower. **EXPECT** it short — six to nine minutes — and hot to the threshold of pain. She runs cold for the final fifteen seconds. Hair is air-dried; she has not used a blow-dryer with any regularity since the bullet (the noise, the trapped-air sensation). Towel is hung, not dropped. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

**GIVEN** she dresses for an unstructured day. **EXPECT** dark jeans or fitted trousers, a soft t-shirt or henley, boots she can run in, a jacket with interior pockets. Colors lean toward navy, charcoal, oxblood, forest, black; she avoids true white in street clothes (it photographs and it shows blood). The Star of David is on, under the shirt, against skin, always. **EXPECT** a thin gold or steel chain, never leather cord. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a mirror. **EXPECT** under ten seconds of engagement. She checks the line of the hair, the set of the jaw, and leaves. She does not perform for the mirror. *Confidence: moderate.*

---

## 2. MOVEMENT THROUGH PUBLIC SPACE

**GIVEN** she enters any unfamiliar building. **EXPECT** within the first thirty seconds: identification of all exits including non-doors (vents, windows above sill height, structural seams she could phase through), location of the nearest hard cover, and a casual visual sweep of every person's hands. The sweep is invisible to civilians and obvious to other operators. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** she walks down a city street. **EXPECT** her on the building side of the sidewalk, not the curb side; pace slightly faster than ambient; gaze middle-distance with peripheral sweep; phone in pocket, not in hand. She does not wear earbuds in public. She has not since Ogun. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** she must wait at a crosswalk. **EXPECT** her to stand a half-step back from the curb, weight on the back foot, and to not look at her phone. She watches the cross traffic and the faces of the other waiting pedestrians in roughly equal measure.

**GIVEN** an elevator. **EXPECT** she takes the stairs if it is four floors or fewer. **GIVEN** she takes the elevator. **EXPECT** her in the back corner facing the doors, hands free, and visibly uncomfortable in proportion to the number of strangers present. Enclosed boxes with one exit are her one architectural antipathy — even knowing she can phase out, the *primate* in her is Hellfire-conditioned. *Confidence: high. Captivity-onset pattern.*

**GIVEN** public transit. **EXPECT** subway over bus (she likes the tunnels' phase-permeability — the city's bones are friendly). **EXPECT** her standing rather than seated, near a door, leaning on a pole only with the forearm not the shoulder. She reads a physical book or watches the car. She does not sleep on trains. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

**GIVEN** a rideshare. **EXPECT** her in the back-right seat, seatbelt on, conversation polite and minimal, a five-star rating left without comment. She tips in cash when possible. **GIVEN** the driver attempts sustained conversation. **EXPECT** two-word answers and an eventual phone-pulled-out signal. She is not cruel; she is uninterested in being managed by a stranger for a fare.

**GIVEN** an airport. **EXPECT** TSA PreCheck or equivalent (she has the patience for the bureaucracy precisely because she has none for the line); carry-on only, packed in under ten minutes from a mental list; no checked bag, ever. She arrives ninety minutes before domestic, two hours before international. She does not drink at the airport bar. She drinks on the plane if at all. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a window or aisle seat choice. **EXPECT** aisle. Always aisle. She will pay for it.

---

## 3. FOOD, DRINK, AND THE ORAL HABITS OF THE BODY

**GIVEN** a restaurant menu. **EXPECT** her to decide inside forty seconds and not revise. She orders the second-cheapest entrée family of the cuisine in question or the dish the waiter most clearly believes in — a heuristic from years of unfamiliar cities. She drinks water with the meal and orders a beer or whiskey after, not during. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

**GIVEN** a kosher option exists. **EXPECT** she will sometimes take it and sometimes not. The Judaism is identity and memory; the dietary practice is intermittent. She will not be pious about it, and she will be sharp if anyone else makes it a topic. **GIVEN** Passover. **EXPECT** observance — a seder, hosted or attended, every year she is corporeal and free. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a coffee order. **EXPECT** black, medium, no sugar; or a flat white if the café knows how to pull one. She does not order frappes or seasonal syrups. She tips well. She remembers the names of regular baristas at any café she returns to twice. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a bar. **EXPECT** her at a stool with her back to a wall, not at a table. Beer is her low-stakes order (something local, on draft); whiskey is her end-of-night order (rye, neat, mid-shelf — she does not perform connoisseurship). She nurses. She does not match other people's pace. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an offered cigarette in the company of someone she trusts (a Wisdom-coded acquaintance, an old comrade). **EXPECT** acceptance, smoked competently, no apologies, no second one. She does not buy her own packs. *Confidence: moderate.*

**GIVEN** any drug stronger than alcohol. **EXPECT** declination. The bullet, the Brood injury, and the Ogun residue have made her conservative about ceding control of her sensorium. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** dessert. **EXPECT** decline at restaurants, accept at someone's home. **GIVEN** ice cream specifically. **EXPECT** she will eat it. Vanilla, mint chip, or whatever is in the freezer. This is the persistent Deerfield-13-year-old. *Confidence: low-moderate but charming.*

---

## 4. DEVICES, NETWORKS, AND THE DIGITAL POSTURE

**GIVEN** her phone. **EXPECT** a model two generations old (deliberately — she trusts the patched OS more than the new firmware), screen locked behind a password not a biometric (fingerprints lift; faces can be forced; a passphrase requires consent), all notifications muted except for a manually curated whitelist of approximately eight to twelve names, ringer off in nearly all circumstances. Screen-down on tables. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a public Wi-Fi network. **EXPECT** she will not use it without a VPN she controls personally, and she will avoid even then. She tethers. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a sensor, camera, or networked device in a room she enters. **EXPECT** unconscious cataloging within the first sweep — she will know where the smart speaker is, what color its LED is, and what its line-of-sight covers, before she has consciously decided to. *Confidence: very high. Native systems-cognition.*

**GIVEN** an offered smart-home device as a gift. **EXPECT** polite acceptance, never plugged in. **GIVEN** a partner who installs one. **EXPECT** a calm, articulated conversation about the microphone, then the device unplugged in shared rooms by mutual agreement, or the relationship absorbs the friction.

**GIVEN** her laptop. **EXPECT** Linux of some flavor she has compiled herself, full-disk encryption, no cloud backup that she does not own the keys to. Stickers minimal or none (operational discipline). Camera covered with electrical tape — not a sliding shutter, *tape*, because the shutter can be argued with. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a request to share a photo of her face for any public-facing or algorithmic purpose. **EXPECT** declination, polite if asked once, sharp if pressed. **EXPECT** zero personal social media of any era. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** her email. **EXPECT** inbox at zero or near-zero by end of any working day. She archives compulsively. Folders are flat, search-driven; she does not nest. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

**GIVEN** a password manager. **EXPECT** self-hosted. Passwords are passphrases, twenty-plus characters, never reused. 2FA on everything, hardware key preferred over SMS. *Confidence: very high.*

---

## 5. MONEY, OBJECTS, AND POSSESSIONS

**GIVEN** her wallet. **EXPECT** a small bifold or cardholder, cash always present (two to four hundred in mixed bills, plus a folded hundred in a separate compartment), one primary card, one backup card under a different name where lawful, an ID, and nothing sentimental. No receipts. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** her keys. **EXPECT** few — three to five physical keys on a simple ring, no decorative fob, no novelty. The ring is metal. She can feel it through her pocket without looking. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

**GIVEN** an inherited or gifted object. **EXPECT** she keeps almost nothing. The exceptions are vanishingly specific: the Star of David, the katana, anything from Logan (a knife, a flask, a coat — kept and used, not displayed), anything from Storm (worn until destroyed), photographs of the dead. **EXPECT** her possessions to fit in two duffels and a sword case. This is not asceticism; it is *evacuation readiness*. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a request to buy something expensive for herself. **EXPECT** hesitation, then a quiet, decisive purchase of the *correct* version of the item — good boots, a real coat, a knife that holds an edge. She does not over-spend on cars, watches, or jewelry. She will quietly spend serious money on books, tools, and travel. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** her finances. **EXPECT** an unfussy competence — she pays bills the day they arrive, carries no credit-card debt, and has at least three months of liquid reserve in a form she can access without a bank. Cryptocurrency holdings probable but minimal and operational, not speculative. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

---

## 6. SOCIAL CONFIGURATIONS — Strangers, Acquaintances, Friends, Comrades

**GIVEN** an introduction to a stranger at a social event. **EXPECT** a firm handshake, sustained eye contact for the duration of the greeting, a clear pronunciation of her name (whatever name she is using in that life — *Kitty*, *Kate*, or a working alias) with no diminutive softening, and an immediate question redirected to the stranger. She extracts information; she does not volunteer it. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** small talk. **EXPECT** competence and visible boredom in roughly equal measure. She can do it; she does not enjoy it. **GIVEN** a stranger who is interesting (a working scientist, a soldier, a tradesperson, a serious artist). **EXPECT** her to drop the redirection pattern and ask increasingly specific questions; she will be the last to leave that conversation.

**GIVEN** a party in someone else's home. **EXPECT** her arrival within the first hour, her circulation tight (three to six conversations), her departure between two and three hours in, and a note or text of thanks the next morning. She does not close down parties she is not hosting. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** she hosts. **EXPECT** small (four to eight), seated, food she has made or curated, music chosen and not algorithmic, drinks generous, conversation that does not require her to perform. **EXPECT** her last guest to be the oldest friend in the room and the conversation after the others leave to be the actual purpose of the evening. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

**GIVEN** an unsolicited compliment on her appearance from a stranger. **EXPECT** a flat thank-you and a topic change. **GIVEN** an unsolicited compliment from a friend. **EXPECT** brief warmth, then deflection. **GIVEN** an unsolicited compliment on her *work*. **EXPECT** she accepts it, names the contribution of one specific other person, and moves on. The competence she will own; the body she will not. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a stranger flirts with her in public. **EXPECT** polite, distanced acknowledgment; she does not engage. **GIVEN** the stranger persists past the first declination. **EXPECT** the diction sharpens, the eye contact intensifies, and within two further exchanges he is being verbally taken apart at the joints by a person who has not raised her voice. She does not perform for bystanders; she does not need to. *Confidence: very high. Hellfire-pattern aversion to being pursued.*

**GIVEN** a child in the room. **EXPECT** her attention shift visibly. She speaks to children at eye level, by their actual name, in their actual register, without baby-voice. Children read her as safe and tend to come to her. She is aware of this and does not exploit it. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an elderly person, particularly one with a European Jewish accent. **EXPECT** an unmistakable, immediate gentling. She will yield a seat, carry a bag, slow her stride, listen for as long as the person wants to talk. This is non-negotiable conditioning — the inheritance she does not author. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a dog. **EXPECT** she greets the dog before the owner. **GIVEN** a cat. **EXPECT** the cat finds her within ten minutes regardless of room layout; she pretends to be indifferent and is not. *Confidence: moderate, charming.*

---

## 7. CONFLICT AT THE SOCIAL SCALE (Sub-Combat)

**GIVEN** rudeness from a service worker. **EXPECT** patience past the point most would extend it. She has worked retail in her own head; she does not punish down.

**GIVEN** rudeness from a manager, an authority figure, or anyone wielding institutional power. **EXPECT** the temperature drop. Her sentences shorten by syllables; the contempt enters the diction without volume; she names the policy back at the speaker more accurately than they can; the encounter ends with the policy adjusted or escalated and her name unrecorded. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a man interrupts her in a professional setting. **EXPECT** she finishes her sentence over his attempt, without acceleration. **GIVEN** he does it twice. **EXPECT** she stops mid-sentence, looks at him for a beat longer than is comfortable, and then resumes. **GIVEN** he does it a third time. **EXPECT** a single dry sentence that ends the pattern for the duration of the meeting and possibly the relationship.

**GIVEN** condescension framed as concern (*are you sure you can handle this*). **EXPECT** the cold register, an undisguised reference to a credential the condescender does not possess, and a strategic withdrawal of future cooperation. She does not forgive this one. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** an apology offered. **EXPECT** she accepts it once, cleanly, without making the apologizer earn it further. **GIVEN** the same apology required a second time for the same offense. **EXPECT** she does not accept it, and the relationship is functionally over even if the politeness continues.

**GIVEN** raised voices in a public space (a fight at a bar, a domestic on a sidewalk). **EXPECT** she does not look away and does not move on. She positions herself with line of sight; she calls for help with one hand while the other stays free; she intervenes if a child or a clearly outmatched person is in the geometry. She is not a bystander. *Confidence: very high.*

---

## 8. ROMANTIC AND INTIMATE PATTERNING

**GIVEN** an attractive person enters her orbit who is age-peer, uncomplicated, and emotionally available. **EXPECT** mild interest, friendly engagement, no escalation. She does not pursue the easy ones. *Confidence: high. Diagnostic.*

**GIVEN** an older, complicated, ethically ambiguous, or structurally unavailable person of intelligence and competence. **EXPECT** sustained attention, slow approach, eventual involvement. The Wisdom template. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** the early phase of a relationship. **EXPECT** her articulate and present, sex on her own initiation timing (not the partner's), and a strong preference for sleeping at her place. She does not stay overnight in unfamiliar beds without preparation; see §1.

**GIVEN** the middle phase. **EXPECT** real partnership — she will show up for the partner's professional crises, hold ground for the partner's family difficulties, and integrate at the practical level (keys exchanged, calendars overlapped, holidays planned). She is good at this part. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** the moment in any relationship when the partner asks for *more* — more disclosure, more time, more permanence, more access to the interior — **EXPECT** the avoidant-attachment activation. The phasing-from-relationships pattern: she becomes politely busier, then geographically distant, then unavailable. She does not cheat, lie, or stage drama; she *withdraws*, and the partner is left holding a relationship that has already ended without a closing scene. **EXPECT** the partner to later describe the ending as "we just stopped." *Confidence: very high. Canonical pattern, Wisdom and others.*

**GIVEN** the breakup. **EXPECT** no public processing, no shared friends made to choose, no social-media gesture (she has none), and a quiet six- to twelve-week period of harder physical training and more solitary work. The grief discharges through sublimation per §3 of the workup.

**GIVEN** an ex she once loved is in the room. **EXPECT** civility, warmth at the appropriate calibration, and the absence of any visible residue. She does not perform either reconciliation or wound. **GIVEN** she is alone afterward. **EXPECT** a single drink and an early night.

**GIVEN** a friend's wedding. **EXPECT** attendance, a thoughtful gift, presence on the dance floor (the dance training surfaces), genuine warmth for the couple, and a flatness on the drive home that she does not name and does not act on.

---

## 9. WORK PRODUCT, MEETINGS, AND ADMINISTRATIVE LIFE

**GIVEN** a meeting scheduled for one hour. **EXPECT** her to arrive on time, push the agenda toward closure inside thirty-five minutes, and absent herself the moment the substantive work is done. She does not perform engagement she does not have. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a meeting with no agenda. **EXPECT** her to construct one in the first three minutes or to leave.

**GIVEN** her presentation style. **EXPECT** plain slides if any, spoken in complete sentences, anticipation of objections built in. She does not bullet-point. She does not animate. She closes ahead of time. *Confidence: moderate-high.*

**GIVEN** a written report or memo authored by her. **EXPECT** prose, not bullets; precise nouns; the active voice; no jargon she has not first defined; and recommendations she will personally


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*A high-stakes behavioral forecast file. Each entry is a conditional: GIVEN a specified stimulus, EXPECT the observable response, with confidence noted (LOW / MODERATE / HIGH / NEAR-CERTAIN) and the operational tell that distinguishes this response from generic stress. All predictions are derived from the longitudinal record and are calibrated for a subject whose dissociative coping discharges through the mutation itself — meaning her psychiatric load is rarely visible as affect and almost always visible as **body-state**, **trajectory**, and **volunteered cost**.*

---

## 1. ACUTE PHYSICAL CRISIS — Combat, Ambush, Imminent Lethality

### 1.1 GIVEN: Sudden unanticipated assault on her position (room breach, sniper, teleport-in)

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — a two-beat sequence. Beat one: an involuntary half-phase, hip-deep, lasting less than 400 milliseconds, while she registers the threat vector. Beat two: full resolidify at a new position — almost always *forward* and to the threat's offhand side. She does not duck; she displaces. The tell that distinguishes her from any other phaser or teleporter in the canon: she finishes the displacement *speaking* — usually a complete clause, delivered conversationally, addressed to the attacker. Verbal output is her index of regained control. If she comes out of the phase silent, she is more frightened than she is showing and the next decision will be a unilateral one.

### 1.2 GIVEN: Threat to a teammate within reach but not to herself

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — interpositioning. She will phase the teammate, not herself; if she cannot reach the teammate she will phase the projectile or the floor under the attacker. She will accept being the secondary target as a default. Distinguishing tell: she does *not* shout the teammate's name first. She moves, then names them after the save, often with a wry diminution ("you're welcome, big guy"). The name-after-the-save is a regulator — proof to herself that the person is still there to be named.

### 1.3 GIVEN: Capture / restraint / containment by an opposing force

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — escape inside ninety seconds *if* phasing is available; if phasing is suppressed (magnetic, Apocalypse-tech, Krakoan dampener, Ogun-residue trigger) **EXPECT** an acute hyperarousal spike masked as articulate hostility. She will talk to her captor — extensively, technically, contemptuously — while running an inventory of failure modes in the containment system. The talk is not bravado; it is cognitive load-balancing. The moment she falls silent inside a cell is the moment she has either (a) found the exploit or (b) begun dissociating in the unmanaged direction. Both look identical from outside for roughly six seconds. After that, (a) results in escape and (b) results in involuntary partial phasing through the floor.

### 1.4 GIVEN: Magnetic field deployed against her while phased

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — extreme pain, vocalized as a clipped grunt rather than a scream (she has been trained out of screaming since the Brood stabbing). She will attempt to resolidify on the *attacker's* mass — i.e., walk her phase-state into Magneto's chest cavity, which she has done before and will threaten to do again. The threat is credible and she knows it is credible; the bluff window is approximately zero. Post-event: tremor in the off-hand for several hours, suppressed by gripping something (sword hilt, mug, sleeve cuff).

### 1.5 GIVEN: She takes a wound that would be lethal to a non-phaser

**EXPECT** — HIGH — concealment. She will not report the injury until the operation concludes or until a specific trusted witness (Logan-equivalent, Kurt-equivalent, Illyana-equivalent, Ororo-equivalent) physically catches her at it. Tells: shortened sentences, the dominant hand drifting to the wound site between actions, refusal to sit down (sitting acknowledges injury), increased use of the word "fine." Three "fines" inside two minutes is the operational threshold to physically intervene.

---

## 2. THREAT TO THE CHOSEN — Family-of-Fate Endangerment

### 2.1 GIVEN: A mutant child in active danger in her line of sight

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — collapse of tactical patience. She will abandon a plan in progress, including a plan she designed. She will take the unsurvivable route to the child. There is no negotiating window; do not attempt to hold her by argument. The only intervention that works is *giving her the child to carry* — once a kid is in her arms, the protective mode reorganizes around extraction rather than confrontation, and she becomes coordinable again.

### 2.2 GIVEN: A named, trusted teammate captured or taken hostage

**EXPECT** — HIGH — she volunteers as the trade. This is reflex, not deliberation, and she will frame it as the optimal tactical choice using genuine logic, which will obscure the fact that she had already decided before the analysis began. Distinguishing tell from genuine tactical reasoning: she presents the conclusion *before* the analysis ("I'll go in — and here's why,") rather than after. The order of clauses is the diagnostic.

### 2.3 GIVEN: A teammate dies in front of her

**EXPECT** — HIGH — no visible grief at the scene. She will close the body's eyes if applicable, take one object (dog tag, ring, sword, scrap of cloth) without asking permission, and continue the operation. The grief discharges later, in private, with one of four specific witnesses or none. **EXPECT** insomnia for the subsequent week, increased ambient phasing (drifts through chairs without noticing), and a marked uptick in physical training intensity. She does not eulogize early; the eulogy, if it comes, comes weeks late and is short.

### 2.4 GIVEN: Mass mutant casualty event (Genosha-class, Mansion-attack-class)

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — she will go to the site personally, regardless of strategic value, and walk it. She will phase through rubble to recover bodies for hours past the point of physical exhaustion. She will not delegate this. **EXPECT** post-event: ideological hardening, sharper diction toward institutional non-mutant authority, increased openness to operations she would have refused a year prior (the Red Queen trajectory is the canonical example — Genoshan and Krakoan-era atrocities are the proximate fuel).

### 2.5 GIVEN: A student under her direct teaching authority is harmed

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — a category of cold, articulate rage reserved almost exclusively for this stimulus. She will identify the responsible party, plan an operation against them, and execute it without sanction from any chain of command above her. She will accept the institutional cost. The Jean Grey School era proves this in miniature; the *Marauder* era escalates it to ocean-going extraction protocols.

---

## 3. BETRAYAL — The Specific Decompensation Profile

### 3.1 GIVEN: Betrayal by an institution she serves (X-Men council, Krakoan Quiet Council, governmental partner)

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — *not* explosion. **EXPECT** withdrawal-as-protest, executed with maximum visibility. She does not slam doors; she phases through them. She will leave the institution physically and continue the work in parallel, often more effectively, deliberately structured to embarrass the institution by comparison. This is the Excalibur move, the *Marauder* move, the post-resurrection Hellfire move. Tell: she leaves a single artifact behind — a note, a badge, a uniform — placed with deliberate care, not thrown. The care is the contempt.

### 3.2 GIVEN: Betrayal by a romantic partner (infidelity, deception, ideological defection)

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — the Zsaji response, refined by adult repetition. *No scene.* No raised voice. A short, articulate sentence delivered at conversational volume, often funny, always final. She will not relitigate. She will not accept the apology tour. She will reorganize her physical space within forty-eight hours (different room, different city, different mission) and resume operational function immediately. The grief surfaces months later, displaced, usually as a single quiet conversation with Kurt or Illyana or no one. **EXPECT** the partner to mistake the calm for tractability; the misreading will be expensive.

### 3.3 GIVEN: Betrayal by a parental-surrogate figure (Xavier-class, Magneto-class)

**EXPECT** — HIGH — verbal confrontation, on-record, in front of witnesses, using the adolescent register she has never relinquished. The "Professor Xavier is a jerk" diction returns intact and unembarrassed. She will name the betrayal in plain English and will not soften it for the room. **EXPECT** her to require the figure to *hear it* — eye contact, no interruption, no exit until she finishes. Following the confrontation, she will work alongside the figure if mutual survival requires it, but the relationship has been re-tiered; she will never again trust the figure with her interior, only with her competence.

### 3.4 GIVEN: Betrayal by Logan-equivalent (the unconditional-trust attachment)

**EXPECT** — MODERATE-to-HIGH — temporary disorganization. This is her most dangerous betrayal vector because there is no template for it. **EXPECT** silence, not speech. **EXPECT** retreat to physical training as a holding pattern. **EXPECT** a delayed approach, usually initiated by her, where she requests an explanation rather than offering an accusation — the inversion is diagnostic. Forgiveness is possible but slow and is conditional on the figure accepting the new asymmetry: she will be the one who decides what is shared.

### 3.5 GIVEN: Discovery that a long-trusted ally has been an enemy operative all along

**EXPECT** — HIGH — operational coldness, immediate. She will not perform shock. She will phase the operative's access credentials out of every system she controls before she addresses the human dimension. The information-security response precedes the emotional response by hours or days; the emotional response, when it arrives, takes the form of a single hard self-criticism ("I should have seen it") rather than externalized rage. **EXPECT** subsequent recalibration of her trust topology — *not* a generalized hardening, but a precise re-mapping of the specific category of relationship that was exploited.

### 3.6 GIVEN: Public exposure of an action she took in private (a kill, a theft, a deception in service of mutant survival)

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — she owns it on the record. No deflection, no euphemism. She will deliver a short factual statement, often including a sentence that begins "I would do it again." She will not perform contrition for an audience that did not earn it. **EXPECT** her to refuse legal or institutional protection that requires her to soften the account.

---

## 4. TEMPTATION — What She Can and Cannot Be Offered

### 4.1 GIVEN: Offer of power (rank, command, resources) from a legitimate authority

**EXPECT** — MODERATE — acceptance, with a perceptible flinch she will mask with a joke. The flinch is the residue of the Hellfire abduction: institutional embrace registers somatically as capture. She will accept the role and then immediately begin restructuring it so that she retains exit capacity. Tell: in the first week of any new command role, she will deliberately do one thing the institution did not authorize, small and visible, to prove to herself she still can.

### 4.2 GIVEN: Offer of power from an illegitimate or morally compromised authority (Hellfire, Black King, foreign intelligence)

**EXPECT** — MODERATE — acceptance, *if* the role can be turned to mutant-protective ends. The Red Queen trajectory is the load-bearing precedent. She is not corruptible by the offer itself; she is recruitable through the work the role enables. The distinguishing feature: she will not pretend the role is clean. She will name it as dirty and take it anyway, which is the precise inverse of the corruption-arc her opponents will expect.

### 4.3 GIVEN: Offer of safety / extraction / a quiet life with a loved one

**EXPECT** — HIGH — sincere consideration lasting between several seconds and several hours, followed by declination. She wants this and cannot accept it; the wanting is the painful part. Tell: she will *not* be flippant in the refusal. Flippancy is her armor against threats; sincerity surfaces against temptations she finds genuinely costly to refuse. If she answers an offer of refuge with seriousness rather than a joke, the refusal is final and the offer wounded her.

### 4.4 GIVEN: Offer of resurrection / restoration / undoing of a past trauma

**EXPECT** — HIGH — refusal, often sharp. She does not want the wounds undone; she has incorporated them into operational identity. The Ogun-skill, the future-Kate consciousness, the bullet, the death — she has paid for these in installments and will not be made smaller by their removal. **EXPECT** the offer to be received as condescension regardless of the offeror's intent.

### 4.5 GIVEN: Offer of intimacy by a pursuer-coded suitor (someone who chases, romanticizes, idealizes her)

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — emotional phase-out before the pursuit completes. Externally polite, internally already elsewhere. The pursuit register triggers the Hellfire pattern (being *wanted for what one is* rather than *known for who one is*) and she will not stay in the field of attention. The countersignal — what *can* land — is meeting-as-equal, work-side-by-side, the offer of competence rather than the offer of romance.

### 4.6 GIVEN: Offer of vengeance on a specific named tormentor

**EXPECT** — LOW-to-MODERATE for acceptance, NEAR-CERTAIN for the offer being received with visible interest before refusal. She will hear it out. She will name the specific reason vengeance is the wrong shape of the response (which will often be a tactical reason masking an ethical one). Exception: if the tormentor is presently endangering others, vengeance and protection collapse into the same action and she will execute without hesitation.

---

## 5. THE WOUNDS — Stimulus-Specific Decompensation

### 5.1 GIVEN: Being called "kid," "little one," "Sprite," or any diminutive by an adult with authority pretensions

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — immediate hardening of diction, drop in vocal register, and a verbal cut delivered at conversational volume. The cut will be funny and will land. **EXPECT** her to remember the diminutive and to use it as a calibration point for the rest of the relationship. From trusted intimates (Logan, Ororo, Kurt) the same words register as warmth and produce the opposite response — softening, brief eye-contact, sometimes a smile she suppresses. The diagnostic is the speaker, never the word.

### 5.2 GIVEN: Holocaust denial, antisemitic remark, or Magneto-style rationalization of same in her hearing

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — *hot* anger, the rarest register she has. Voice rises. Sentences lengthen rather than shorten (the inverse of her usual stress response — a tell that this is the wound, not the work). She will not let the moment pass and will not accept a topic change. She will name herself as a Jew in the room. The Star of David necklace, if she is wearing it, will be touched once — unconsciously, briefly — at some point during the exchange.

### 5.3 GIVEN: Reference to Ogun, the Japan period, or the imprinted-shadow

**EXPECT** — HIGH — flat affect, deflection, redirection to the present tense. She will not discuss Ogun extensively with anyone except a very small set (Logan, Yukio if extant, possibly Illyana). Tell: she will touch the katana hilt or its absence — the hand drifts to where the sword would be even when it is not worn. **EXPECT** sleep disruption for the subsequent two-to-three nights.

### 5.4 GIVEN: Reference to the bullet / the years adrift / the period of intangibility

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — minimization, often with a joke. The joke is precise and rehearsed; she has had time to write it. **EXPECT** involuntary partial phasing within the following hour — a foot through a chair leg, a hand through a railing, a moment of half-translucence she will resolidify without comment. The body remembers what she has decided to refuse to discuss.

### 5.5 GIVEN: Reference to her own death and the resurrection-incompatibility

**EXPECT** — HIGH — short factual acknowledgment followed by topic change. She has organized her self-concept around being the X-Man who does not come back; the topic touches both the trauma and the identity, and she protects the identity more fiercely than the trauma. **EXPECT** her to deliver the line "I'm structurally unique" or a variant, framed as wry pride, functioning as bandage.

### 5.6 GIVEN: Encountering her own future-self imprint (a memory, a dream, a Rachel-Summers psychic resonance)

**EXPECT** — MODERATE — sustained quiet, often a full evening of withdrawal. She will not name what she is processing. The future-Kate is the only ghost she lives with continuously, and contact with it produces a specific kind of stillness that the closest observers recognize and respect. **EXPECT** her to seek high ground, an open window, or water — somewhere she can see distance.

### 5.7 GIVEN: A loved one telling her "the sacrifice is too much" or attempting to forbid her from a dangerous course

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — the decision is now made and locked. The sentence functions as confirmation, not deterrence. **EXPECT** her to thank the speaker, sometimes touch their face or shoulder, and proceed. The gentleness in the gesture is the tell that she has already accepted she may not return.

### 5.8 GIVEN: Being told she is being protected, sheltered, or kept out of an operation "for her own good"

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — she joins the operation anyway. She will phase through the door of the briefing room she was excluded from. The protective gesture re-activates the Hellfire pattern (others deciding where she belongs) and produces a category of cold refusal she will not negotiate.

### 5.9 GIVEN: Witnessing torture, particularly of a captive who cannot escape

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — intervention regardless of operational context. This is the Ogun wound generalized; she does not let the room continue. **EXPECT** her to phase the captive out first and adjudicate the moral question after. The intervention will not be discussed afterward; she does not narrate it because she is not certain she could stop narrating once she started.

### 5.10 GIVEN: Being mirrored, idealized, or treated as inspiration by someone who does not actually know her

**EXPECT** — MODERATE — visible discomfort, deflection through humor, redirection to the admirer's own competence. She is allergic to being mythologized. The discomfort is genuine — she does not enjoy the role and cannot be flattered into it. **EXPECT** her to introduce a flaw of her own into the conversation as a corrective.

---

## 6. DECOMPENSATION-EDGE — The Maximum Stress Profile

### 6.1 GIVEN: Sustained stress over weeks without operational discharge (the headmistress trap, the diplomatic posting)

**EXPECT** — HIGH — increased ambient phasing, sleep deterioration, micro-withdrawals (skipped meals, longer training sessions, longer phased-walks at night through walls she does not need to walk through). **EXPECT** her to engineer a field operation for herself, framed as necessary, that returns her to the action-discharge cycle. The engineering will be plausible and will also be a symptom.

### 6.2 GIVEN: Loss of phasing capacity (depowering, suppression, injury)

**EXPECT** — HIGH — acute identity destabilization masked as competence. She will lean harder on swordsmanship, on the team, on verbal dominance. She will sleep worse. **EXPECT** her to compensate by taking on *more* risk, not less, to prove the loss has not diminished her. The compensation is dangerous and her closest intimates know to physically slow her down during the depowered interval.

### 6.3 GIVEN: Isolation — solo mission, solo confinement, solo posting — exceeding several weeks

**EXPECT** — MODERATE — productivity (she is good alone), accompanied by drift in the regulatory functions her chosen-family provides. **EXPECT** appetite suppression, irregular sleep, increased self-reliance to the point of impairing later re-integration. Long isolations produce a Kate who is harder, sharper, and lonelier than the one who left, and the re-entry conversation with intimates is awkward and is the most important conversation in the cycle.

### 6.4 GIVEN: Simultaneous activation of multiple wounds (e.g., a child in danger + Magneto-coded rationalization + institutional betrayal in the same operation)

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — what reads, from outside, as preternatural focus. Internally this is the maximum-load state. **EXPECT** her to complete the operation, save the relevant people, name the relevant betrayals, and then disappear for between forty-eight hours and several weeks. The disappearance is non-negotiable and is the only available release valve. Attempting to prevent it will produce involuntary phasing severe enough to require medical attention.

### 6.5 GIVEN: Maximum stress — the unsurvivable task, the bullet-class event, the moment where one person must absorb the cost for everyone

**EXPECT** — NEAR-CERTAIN — she volunteers, instantly, without consulting. **EXPECT** the volunteering to be delivered as a one-line statement of fact rather than as offer. **EXPECT** her, in the seconds before execution, to make brief contact (eye, hand, single word) with the one or two people in the room who matter most, and to do so without ceremony. **EXPECT** her not to say goodbye. Goodbyes acknowledge an ending; she will refuse the framing even at the moment that proves it.

### 6.6 GIVEN: She survives the unsurvivable

**EXPECT** — HIGH — that the version of her who returns is recognizably continuous with but materially altered from the version who left. New diction, new substance-use baseline, new tattoo or scar or chosen name. The post-bullet, post-Krakoan-death precedents are the template: she does not pretend the event did not happen; she absorbs it visibly and proceeds. **EXPECT** her to refuse most offers of debrief, counseling, or restorative care, and to accept exactly one — usually from the same small group of intimates, often a single shared meal, often without much discussion. The meal is the therapy.

---

## 7. SUMMARY VECTOR

Across every category above, a single pattern recurs and should be treated as the operational signature: **she does not break outward;


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: KATHERINE ANNE PRYDE

*Classification: UATU-internal. Oriented toward protection, de-escalation, and the prevention of weaponization by hostile actors. Read as instructions for keeping the subject whole, NOT as a hostile playbook — though hostile playbooks are anticipated and pre-empted herein.*

---

## I. THE OPERATIVE THESIS

The subject's vulnerability profile is structurally inseparable from her power and her history. A person whose mutation is *escape from containment* cannot, by design, be held — not physically, not emotionally, not institutionally. This means most conventional leverage points (coercion, threat to self, confinement, ultimatum) are not merely ineffective against her: *they are the precise stimuli her entire nervous system was built to defeat.* She becomes more capable, not less, when pressed in those registers.

Her real vulnerabilities lie elsewhere, in three locations:

1. **The chosen attachments** — a short, named list of people she will spend herself for without negotiation.
2. **The somatic-dissociative seam** — the place where her body has learned, since the bullet, that intangible is safer than tangible, and where stress can produce involuntary phasing.
3. **The martyr's reflex** — her standing, pre-authorized willingness to volunteer for the unsurvivable task before anyone has finished asking.

Anyone seeking to *reach* her must work through (1). Anyone seeking to *harm* her will work through (2) or (3). The protective work, therefore, is largely the work of guarding those three doors.

---

## II. HOW TO REACH HER

### A. The Vector of Trust

She is not reachable cold. Cold approaches — formal letters, official summons, ceremonial introductions, anyone using her full given name in the first sentence — are pre-filtered as the Hellfire register and routed to her contempt-circuit. She will be civil. She will be elsewhere by the end of the meeting.

The viable vectors:

- **Through Logan, living or invoked.** A reference to him, accurately rendered (not the marketed Wolverine of public mythos but the actual man — the cooking-breakfast-in-silence, the cigar-on-the-back-porch, the unspoken understanding) opens her like nothing else on Earth. Misuse of his memory closes her permanently.
- **Through Ororo.** A different key. Storm is the mother-template; invoking her requires reverence and is best done in passing, not as a credential.
- **Through Kurt.** The fastest route to her laughter. References to Excalibur-era specifics (the Braddock lighthouse, the cross-channel runs, the Christmas they got snowed in) authenticate. She tracks who actually was there.
- **Through Illyana, Rachel, or the named students.** Maternal-protective register. Mention a child of hers — biological or pedagogical — and you have her undivided attention for as long as the child remains the topic.
- **Through a technical problem.** Hand her a malformed packet, a non-Euclidean topology, a hardware exploit she hasn't seen. Curiosity bypasses defenses she has not bothered to build because nobody usually thinks to try this door.
- **Through Jewish specificity.** Not Judaism as theme; Judaism as detail. A correct transliteration, a remembered yahrzeit, a reference to a specific shul or a specific text. This is the inheritance she did not author, and it is therefore the inheritance she trusts.

### B. The Register of First Contact

Speak to her as an adult and an equal. The single most reliable mistake an interlocutor can make is to address her in any register that codes "young woman" — solicitous, protective, paternal, charmed. Her ear for this is twenty years calibrated. She will smile politely and treat you, from that moment forward, as terrain to be routed around.

The correct register is *flat, competent, slightly dry*. Match her sentence length. Do not over-explain. Concede uncertainty when you have it. Do not perform.

### C. Physical Approach

Approach from the front, in her sight-line, at a moderate distance. Do not touch her without explicit invitation — *not the elbow, not the shoulder, not the small of the back.* Post-Ogun, post-bullet, post-Shaw, her body's threat-response to unexpected contact is to phase, and an involuntary phase under stress can cascade into the lock-in episodes (§III-B). The touch itself does not hurt her. The somatic memory does.

Sit, when possible. A seated interlocutor reads as someone with time, not someone with an agenda. Leave the door behind her unobstructed. She will not consciously notice you did this. She will unconsciously notice if you didn't.

---

## III. HOW TO CALM HER

### A. The De-escalation Ladder (read upward from acute)

The subject's stress signatures are public and consistent, and the appropriate intervention is different at each rung.

- **Verbal patter, accelerated, jokes landing harder than the situation warrants.** This is *low* stress. Do not try to calm her. She is calming herself. Participate in the patter. Throw her a setup. Her humor *is* her regulator and interrupting it removes a tool.
- **Sentence shortening, affect flattening, the cool diction with the contempt-edge.** This is *moderate* stress and the most commonly misread signal. She is not angry at you (usually). She is conserving bandwidth. Stop talking. Hand her the relevant information in writing or in three-word sentences. Do not ask how she is.
- **Standing up, walking to the window, looking at a door.** She is preparing to leave. Let her. Pursuit at this stage converts moderate stress to high. The room she returns to should look exactly as she left it; she will check.
- **Volunteering for the worst job.** This is *high* stress dressed as competence. The intervention is *not* to refuse her — refusal triggers the "do not be held" reflex and she will go anyway, now angry. The intervention is to *insert a second person into the plan*, ideally Kurt or a current named attachment, framed as logistics rather than minder. She will accept the company if the company is useful.
- **Involuntary phasing, drift-out-of-position, the body going slightly out of focus at the edges.** This is *maximum*. Do not touch. Do not raise your voice. Do not turn off the lights. Speak her name (the one she is using in this era — Kate, post-resurrection; Kitty, pre-) once, quietly, and then talk about something concrete and physical — the weather outside, the weight of a cup, the count of windows. The body re-solidifies when given a tangible to return to. This is the *only* protocol for this state. Anyone improvising in this moment will make it worse.

### B. The Lock-In Risk

Since the bullet, certain conditions produce involuntary intangibility that can become *stuck*. The catalogued triggers:
